text:
Awesome, with a few minor adjustments I made. Instead of using an onion soup mix, I sauteed 1/2 chopped onion and 1/2 chopped pepper in some butter for about 15 minutes. Then I mixed with the rest of the ingredients. I only used about 1/2 cup of lite sour cream. It turned out absoultely delicious! I'm not usually one for meatloaf since it tends to turn out dry & crumbly, too salty or too greasy and most have a ketchup topping to make it appear moist(not a fave). But this recipe was a great basis for a moist and hearty loaf, and with the alterations I made it is definitely a keeper!

Made this last night and it was yummy!  Used other's suggestions and put in 1/2 c. sour cream, and 1/2 c. ranch dressing.  Also, I only used 3/4 c. of bread crumbs, and 1/2 pkg. of the soup mix, added a splash of A-1 and Tabasco.  Served with mashed potaoes and fresh corn off the cob.  Will definitely make this one again!

text:
This is a really good recipe!  Meatloaf has never been a favorite of mine, but this is delicious.
I added a few touches that my mom always used when she made meatloaf.....I sliced 4-5 potatoes into 1/4" rounds and layered them around the meatloaf, and then poured a can of tomato sauce over the whole thing before covering in foil and baking.

text:
Let me preface by saying that I HATE MEATLOAF and refuse to eat it, but make it about once a month to please my husband and kids.  Now after sayng that, this was the best meatloaf ever!  I actually ate an entire slice and went back for seconds!  My husband and kids love the flavor and have requested I replace my old recipe with this one.  I doubled the recipe, except for the sour cream and onion soup mix...used the quantities call for in the original recipe since other reviews commented that those two ingredients needed to be cut in half.  Also, I added about a 2 Tbsp of Heinz 57, a Tbsp of Dijon mustard and about 1/4 cup of beef broth.  It's a keeper!

I've never made meatloaf before and decided to make this for my wife tonight.  The meatloaf was excellent.  The only thing that confused me was that it didn't call for ketchup.  Every meatloaf I've eaten was cooked with ketchup on top.

I was afraid that it would come out too dry because of the crumbs and onion mix, but the consistency came out well.

Also, the recipe made about 6 servings rather than 12 servings.  But, I'll have to say that this is my new meatloaf recipe to use.

This turned out fantastic! I did make some changes so heres what I did
I used 1/2 cup of sour cream and 1/2 cup of ranch dressing. I used crackers and toast instead of the italian-style bread crumbs, and I put a glaze on top 45 minutes into baking made of 1/4cup of ketchup 1 tbs of mustard and 2tbs of brown sugar 

I didnt have tinfoil so I didnt cover it and it was still moist and perfect.

I have no complaints with this receipe it was very delicious!

text:
I like my regular meatloaf recipe, but wanted to try something different. I read the other reviews and so decided to tweak this just a little. I had about 1 1/4 lbs of ground beef, so other than the egg, used slightly less than the full measures of the other ingredients. And because some said the whole envelope of soup made it too salty, I first mixed the dry soup with a pint of sour cream and made onion dip. I then used slightly less than a cup of the dip in place of the sour cream and the envelope of soup. I also made a ketchup, mustard and brown sugar topping - just kind of guessing at the amount of each. The result was really tasty. Will definitely make this again.

Excellent flavor and texture.  I was so hungry for a good meatloaf and saw a positive review for this one.  I used 2 lbs of very lean ground beef and still only 1/2 a packet of the onion soup mix.  Otherwise, upped the other ingredients as written.  I can't believe there was not any salt or pepper but it's still full of flavor. I baked the 2 lbs for 45 minutes covered, uncovered for 15 minutes and then topped with some squirts of ketchup for another 15 minutes.  Perfectly done and very delicious.  Thanks so much for posting your recipe!

text:
Husband and kids thought this was very good.  I don't really like meatloaf so it's hard for me to personally judge, however, it was definately better than most meatloaves I have tasted and had a good texture. My slight changes: added ground pork, 1/2 pack of ranch dressing mix (based on users who added ranch dressing) and I used plain bread crumbs because that's all I had.   I did also put ketchup on top toward the end (more for appearance) and served with mashed potatoes and beef/tomato gravy.  It smelled wonderful while it was in the oven.  The cook time/temp were perfect, but I don't think 12 servings is accurate...that's only 1.5 ounces of beef per person.   Good recipe!

Probably the best meatloaf I've tasted (and I made it!!). I did not put but 1/2 cup of breadcrumbs based on another review.  When I took off the foil (per the recipe) I put the following on top: In a small bowl, combine 1/2 cup ketchup, 1/2 cup brown sugar, 1 tablespoon lemon juice and 1 teaspoon mustard powder. Make sure you drain off the excess fat before you do this. I also put hot & spicy Allegro in the mixture instead of Worcestershire sauce. Delicious.

text:
Hats off to Eileen for this excellent, easy recipe.  I have made a couple of modifications that may be of interest.  1/2 ground beef and 1/2 ground pork or chicken.  I use plain bread crumbs, and add 1 TBSP Italian Seasoning.  After it is in the loaf pan, I "frost" it with Ketchup, and lay strips of bacon over the top.  After baking 45 minutes, I take the foil off and bake it for another 45.  This meatloaf is a guaranteed hit no matter who I serve it to.  I serve it with either baked yam, baked potato, mashed potatoes and gravy, and a green veggie (green beans go well).

text:
Meatloaf?  How exciting can that be???  This is the BEST!  I've always liked meatloaf and my family...they could take it or leave it.  Since I've started making this one, it is a weekly request.  

I do make a couple of changes.  I add chopped onion, at least a half of a cup.  I omit a pound of beef and add a pound of ground pork and if I can find it, I also add about a pound of ground veal.  I add about a teaspoon of nutmeg, I know it sounds crazy, but try it!  And best of all...you've got to do this!  Chop one half pound of bacon, cook it to crispy, drain and add to the meatloaf ingriedents! WOW! It is SO good!

text:
This is my go-to meatloaf recipe. While many reviewers feel the need to tweak it to their own specific tastes, I can tell you without reservations that no changes are necessary. During the last 10 minutes, I do like to top it with a little BBQ sauce. Again, just a preference. One of the best things about it is that leftovers freeze so very well. I like to vacuum-seal individual slices for later. A suggestion for anyone who dislikes mixing the loaf by hand is to use your KitchenAid at it's lowest speed to combine the ingredients. I don't think I'd ever go back to mixing yucky meat by hand.

Great variation on meatloaf,  and there are many.  I used 1 lb lean hamburger and half lb. italian sausage.  1 16 0z. light sour cream.  2 onion soup pkg.  several tb. spoons worchshire. 2 eggs.
Cup and half italian bread crumbs. 1 diced onion and a minced jap for a kick.  Salt and pepper.  Cooked @ 350 for about an hour covered.  Topped with tomato sauce cooked uncovered another 15 minutes.  The result was a giant italian
meatball in the form of a meatloaf.  Very good !!!  Makes good sandwiches or crumble for pizza topping.

text:
This meatloaf tasted great. This was only the second time I've ever had meatloaf, and the first time I've ever made it. I was happy it didn't look like other meatloafs, with a ketchupy/tomatoey glazed look to it - which I find unappealing. The only thing I changed was to add a couple of squirts of ketchup into the mix. I also discovered I didn't have the bread crumbs I thought I had. Since I'd already mixed everything else together, I had to improvise by using hot dog buns. I used four and tore them each into two sections, placed them on a cookie sheet, and toasted them for a few minutes in the oven at 375 (this would have probably worked better in a toaster oven.) I then crumbled/tore them up into the mix. They weren't *completely* toasted/crisped through, but they worked in place of the bread crumbs. The meatloaf still tasted great. I also didn't think it was too salty, but I am a person who LOVES salt... so I'd say whether it's too salty or not may be purely dependent upon your tastebuds.

This was very good. Also good with ranch dip instead of the sour cream.
 I think a few people confused ranch sour cream dip with ranch dressing, which would add a lot more fat and only make it more greasy.
 I did use less bread crumbs, which can make meatloaf dry and mealy if too much is used as "filler". 
The onion soup mix is the key to it being juicy and not dry also.

I've made this many times and it is my husband's favorite, however tonight it was exceptionally good.  I use about 2+ lbs of ground chuck, 2 eggs, 1 cup of the breadcrumbs, and about 1 cup of sour cream, plus the other ingredients as stated.  I mixed all the ingredients together first  then add them to the gr. beef. I form it into a loaf in a baking pan and let it cook for about a good hour covered then uncovered for about 1/2 hour or so, then top with a mixture of ketchup and brown sugar for about 10 min.  This takes some time to cook through.

text:
It was such an easy recipe to follow and so quick to put together. I did make a few small changes but I think the recipe as written would be good too. I read some of the other suggestions so I used 1/2 cup sour cream and 1/2 ranch dressing. I think the ranch gave it a nice added flavor. I also used 1/4 cup less of the bread crumbs because I thought it might turn out too dry. After baking though, I think the full amount would have been fine. It has a really good flavor and it'll make great sandwiches because it isn't crumbly at all. I'll definately make this again!
